<div id="review_1369124484" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1369124484" />
    <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl"><img alt="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603085284p2/8734459.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1369124484?book_show_action=true">Aug 20, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl">Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=you-go-girl-kickass-heroine">you-go-girl-kickass-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1369124484" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18329765488278538964"><i>Truthwitch</i> is kind of standard YA romantic fantasy, but not bad if you like that kind of thing. Review first posted on <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.FantasyLiterature.com'>www.FantasyLiterature.com:</a><br/><br/><i>Truthwitch</i> starts off <i>in media res</i>, in the midst of a failed heist, and the resulting armed clash and escape are highly dramatic (even if it's not entirely clear at the time what's going on). At the same time, it’s hard to escape the feeling that this is yet another typical young adult romantic fantasy, complete with a teenage kickass heroine (except th</span>
  <span id="freeText18329765488278538964" style="display:none"><i>Truthwitch</i> is kind of standard YA romantic fantasy, but not bad if you like that kind of thing. Review first posted on <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.FantasyLiterature.com">www.FantasyLiterature.com:</a><br /><br /><i>Truthwitch</i> starts off <i>in media res</i>, in the midst of a failed heist, and the resulting armed clash and escape are highly dramatic (even if it's not entirely clear at the time what's going on). At the same time, it’s hard to escape the feeling that this is yet another typical young adult romantic fantasy, complete with a teenage kickass heroine (except this time ― bonus! ― you get two of them!), with unique magical powers that make them highly special and sought-after, and unrealistically awesome sword-fighting techniques. As well, there’s the obligatory instant attraction between one of the girls and a prince, with their relationship jump-started by an intricate and steamy dance that, I have to admit, left me fanning myself.<br /><br /> The world-building in <i>Truthwitch</i> has some creative fantasy aspects to it, but isn’t explored or explained clearly enough, and the lack of details sometimes hurt the story. Key concepts like “thread-cutting” and “cleaving” were inadequately explained, as was the virulent prejudice against Iseult’s people.<br /><br /> The deep friendship and loyalty between the two girls, Safiya and Iseult, is laudatory in a genre that too often shorts true friendship between women. But at the same time, this friendship is the source of much frustration. It’s too similar to the obsessive romantic relationships that show up in too many young adult novels, except here it’s between two girls who, although not romantically involved, are still overly reliant on each other. Their relationship goes beyond loyalty and tips over into co-dependent behavior that tosses aside reason and logic. That aspect of the story is quite irritating.<br /><br /> A large part of this problem is caused by Safiya’s immaturity and impetuousness. Again and again Safi makes idiotic decisions that needlessly endanger herself and Iseult, usually because she thinks someone is going to separate her from Iseult and that Simply. Cannot. Be. My frustration with Safi culminated when a great many people have put themselves at risk to save her, whisking her out of town in secrecy, and Safi freaks out and breaks away from her hiding place, nearly causing the deaths of herself and others … once again, just because she can’t bear the thought of being separated for a while from Iseult. Impulsive heroines ― or heroes ― who make stupid decisions because of their strong feelings are, at least to me, much less appealing than the cool, calculating types. In fairness, Safi does realize the error of her reckless ways toward the end of the novel, but by then it was hard to muster up much sympathy for her, and it felt like a rather obvious plot turn.<br /><br /><i>Truthwitch</i> left me with mixed emotions: at times my reading of it was perfunctory, with me feeling that I’ve read too many books similar to this, but then fairly often a plot twist or character would surprise me with some unexpected depth and the book would recapture my imagination. Between that and the quick, exciting pace of most of the story, <i>Truthwitch</i> will find a large fan base, particularly among teenage and young adult women who like fantasies with kickass heroines and hot guys (especially if they're princes).<br /><br />* * * * *<br /><br /><b>Initial post</b> (after reading the first third of the book):<br />The first 30 or 40% of this upcoming fantasy novel is [was] available on NetGalley, so I downloaded and read it last night. It started off feeling like yet another typical YA fantasy: Yep, there's another kickass heroine ... or two. And they both have special snowflake magical powers aside from their really awesome sword-fighting techniques. And here's a magical kingdom, and of course multiple sinister people who want to capture our heroines and use them for their own nefarious purposes.<br /><br />So I was reading it, a little perfunctorily, and it just wasn't really sucking me in or capturing my imagination. Until all of a sudden it was. <br /><br />I'm not sure what exactly happened, but it involved a couple of characters unexpectedly turning <b>awesome</b>, and an intricate dance with a prince that was pretty amazing and also pretty hot (the dance, I mean, although come to think of it I could also say "the prince" here), and an assassin who may be evil or may be just misguided, but in any case we're not done with him, not by a long shot. And the deep friendship between the two female main characters is unusual in this genre.<br /><br />And now I <i>really</i> want to read the rest of the story. Even though it's the first book and the series is expected to include four books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18329765488278538964" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1441580141" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1441580141" />
    <a title="Mikee (ReadWithMikee)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44137919-mikee-readwithmikee"><img alt="Mikee (ReadWithMikee)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583262285p2/44137919.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1441580141?book_show_action=true">Nov 13, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mikee (ReadWithMikee)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mikee (ReadWithMikee)" href="/user/show/44137919-mikee-readwithmikee">Mikee (ReadWithMikee)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/25187640-truthwitch">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1441580141" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13669517447529058388"><blockquote>
  <i>"I guard the light-bringer,<br/>And protect the dark-giver.<br/>I live for the world-starte,<br/>And die for the shadow-ender.<br/>My blood, I offer freely.<br/>My Threads, I offer wholly.<br/>My eternal soul belongs to no one else.<br/>Claim my Aether.<br/>Guide my blade.<br/>From now until the end."</i>
</blockquote><br/><b>I AM OBSESSED WITH TRUTHWITCH.</b> It was on my <b>
  <i>top ten most anticipated releases of 2016</i>
</b> and it <b>DID NOT</b> disappoint one bit. I can already tell that this series is going to become one of my favorite series of all time because, guys, this w</span>
  <span id="freeText13669517447529058388" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>"I guard the light-bringer,<br />And protect the dark-giver.<br />I live for the world-starte,<br />And die for the shadow-ender.<br />My blood, I offer freely.<br />My Threads, I offer wholly.<br />My eternal soul belongs to no one else.<br />Claim my Aether.<br />Guide my blade.<br />From now until the end."</i>
</blockquote><br /><b>I AM OBSESSED WITH TRUTHWITCH.</b> It was on my <b>
  <i>top ten most anticipated releases of 2016</i>
</b> and it <b>DID NOT</b> disappoint one bit. I can already tell that this series is going to become one of my favorite series of all time because, guys, this world is <b>
  <u>fantastic!</u>
</b><br /><br />Okay, I'll be completely honest with you. I had a little bit of a <b>
  <u>rough start</u>
</b> with this book in the beginning up until about 150 pages in. At first, it felt <b>
  <i>info-dumpy</i>
</b> because of all the <b>names, terms, and bits of history</b> that were thrown our way and it was, I kid you not, <b>
  <i>A LOT</i>
</b> to remember and take in. I appreciated how fast-paced this book was but it felt like Susan Dennard just thrusted us into this world of witches and magic and expected us to know this universe and how it works right off the bat. <br /><br />Sometimes I'm a bit <b>
  <i>slow</i>
</b> when it comes to taking in different worlds that are introduced to me in books, so unfortunately the beginning did not really work out for me the way I hoped it would. For me, it felt like I opened up the book and started right at the middle of the story with everything going on at once without any prior knowledge as to <b>
  <i>who, what, where, and why</i>
</b> this is all happening. I was absolutely fascinated by the Witchlands and all the different types of witches but I did not quite understand what or why the characters were doing what they were doing. But thankfully, everything just starts melding together and making sense as you keep reading. I still found myself <b>
  <u>confused</u>
</b> at times as the story progressed but not to the extent of how it was in the beginning. Hopefully, Susan Dennard <b>
  <i>clarifies</i>
</b> everything by the second installment.<br /><br />I do hope that we get an <b>index, glossary, or something along those lines</b> in the second book that clarify and define certain terms and concepts used in Truthwitch. The Witchlands is a vast world full of different types of witches, even including <b>
  <u>subcategories or subtypes</u>
</b> of a certain type of witch. For example, a <b>Windwitch</b> can strictly control only the wind. An <b>Airwitch,</b> from my understanding, also possesses that same power along with a variety of other abilities such as controlling the air that flows through an individual's lungs, whereas a Windwitch does not. A short, little page in the back of the book or something can go a long way to avoid confusion!<br /><br />Aside from the mixup, I was <b>
  <i>blown away</i>
</b> by this book. It met all my expectations and was every bit as exciting as I thought it would be. I devoured this book and every page kept me turning for the next! I <b>LOVED</b> our main heroines, Safiya and Iseult. They were just <b>
  <i>badass</i>
</b> when it came to their magic and fighting skills. I enjoyed the fact that although they couldn't use their magic to fight back against their opponents, they manage to still defend themselves with their wielded weapons. Of course, I also loved our male characters, Merik and Aeduan. I can't wait to see these four main characters actually working together because I can already tell they're going to be <b>
  <i>squad goals!</i>
</b> And maybe even couple goals. (; I'm already on the Merik and Safina ship 100%, but I think I might be sensing an Iseult and Aeduan relationship in the future as well. &lt;3<br /><br />Thank you Susan Dennard for creating this book and this world. I've been waiting for a book about witches so thank you for giving us that! Like I said, it was a rough start for me but that didn't hold me back from enjoying the story. I'm already dying to find out what else Susan has up her sleeve because this series is awesome guys. I highly recommend Truthwitch and if you're like me and end up struggling through the beginning, <b>
  <i>keep reading and persevere</i>
</b> because it's worth it to stick around until the end.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13669517447529058388" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1453492736" />
    <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four"><img alt="Robin (Bridge Four)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473392517p2/14105531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1453492736?book_show_action=true">Nov 27, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin (Bridge Four)" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four">Robin (Bridge Four)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=4-5-stars">4-5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=fantastic-fantasy">fantastic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=chick-i-want-to-hang-out-with">chick-i-want-to-hang-out-with</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=o-captain-my-captain">o-captain-my-captain</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=kick-ass-heroines">kick-ass-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=witches-warlocks-and-magic">witches-warlocks-and-magic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1453492736" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13591547796145331429"><b>Sale Alert: Kindle deal Jun 8- Jun 14 <a href='https://www.amazon.com/Truthwitch-Witchlands-Novel-Book-ebook/dp/B00Z5Z5NNO/ref=sr_1_21?dchild=1&qid=1591641743&s=digital-text&sr=1-21' rel='nofollow noopener'>$2.99</a></b><br/><br/><b>You want to know what there is a distinct lack of in Fantasy in my opinion???</b> Strong female friendships. I’m not talking about sisters or girls who grew up together but real friendships where you feel so strongly for that other person that no one could ever come between that. Not some boy or culture or a coming war. <br/><br/> <b>The beauty of Truthwitch for me was the relationship between Safi and Iseult.</b> Each would die for the other without a second thought to it.</span>
  <span id="freeText13591547796145331429" style="display:none"><b>Sale Alert: Kindle deal Jun 8- Jun 14 <a href="https://www.amazon.com/Truthwitch-Witchlands-Novel-Book-ebook/dp/B00Z5Z5NNO/ref=sr_1_21?dchild=1&amp;qid=1591641743&amp;s=digital-text&amp;sr=1-21" rel="nofollow noopener">$2.99</a></b><br /><br /><b>You want to know what there is a distinct lack of in Fantasy in my opinion???</b> Strong female friendships. I’m not talking about sisters or girls who grew up together but real friendships where you feel so strongly for that other person that no one could ever come between that. Not some boy or culture or a coming war. <br /><br /> <b>The beauty of Truthwitch for me was the relationship between Safi and Iseult.</b> Each would die for the other without a second thought to it. They would follow the other anywhere in the world and they are stronger together than they ever are apart even though they are from such different backgrounds. <br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Safi had her title to protect her, and Iseult had her heritage to damn her.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br />I loved how indignant and angry Safi got every time that someone judged or insulted Iseult because of the color of her skin and where she was from. Even when Iseult accepts the prejudices of others and lets it roll off Safi never does. They are best friends and maybe more (<i>magically speaking not romantically speaking</i>) and they are incredibly fierce in their protections of each other.<br /><br /><b>There are plenty of other things to like in the story though.</b><br /><br />✧ Interesting new magic.✧<br /><br />Some of the magic reminded me a little of the Grisha series by Leigh Bardugo. In that there are people who can control the Wind, Storms, Tides, Blood, Iron etc…. But it is different because there are people like Safi who is like a human lie detector and can tell when someone isn’t being honest. But Iseult’s power is the one I really wanted. She can see the emotions of people. Different colors mean different things and she can see them as threads around the individuals seeing who is tied to whom.<br /><blockquote>
  <i> For a heartbeat … then two, the space between Merik and Safi—the Threads burning between them—ignited into a full flaming Thread of scarlet. But Iseult had no time to distinguish the exact shade—if it was a growing Thread of love or one of unforgiving hate— </i>
</blockquote><br />✦ A little bit of romance ✦<br /><br />I almost always need a little smidgen of romance in the books I read. I don’t necessarily want it to overshadow the entire story but I love the slow burn of a romance if it is done right and so I very much enjoyed the dance between Safi and Merik. Don’t worry Safi never goes all damsel in distress and becomes a bumbling idiot just because she has an attraction to a man. Instead she buts heads with him, meets his dance move for move and keeps him on his toes wondering what she will pull next. It is a slow burn through to book but when they ignite it is HOT. <br /><blockquote>
  <i> Something had happened between Safi and Merik during their dance. Something as powerful as the wind and the music that had gusted around them. A shift in the air that preceded a storm.</i>
</blockquote><br />I’m also going to say that there is another potential couple I really like the idea of and it is Iseult with Aeduan. Although since he is the enemy in this book it might take some time to bring him to their side. But more on Aeduan later.<br /><br />✧ Brand New World ✧<br /><br />One of the things I really love about fantasy is that you always get a new world to explore. Truthwitch has all that in new lands, cultures and peoples. I enjoyed learning a little about them in this book. We only get to see a few of the places in this world but I’m sure that it will grow even larger as the series continues. We have only seen one of the 5 Magical Wells mentioned so far but I can’t wait to see what happens to this world if Safi and Iseult can figure out how to get them working.<br /><br />✦ The Bad Guys ✦<br /><br />There are a few and they all seem very dangerous. There are also a few people that I’m not sure what side they are playing on yet and so it will be interesting to see if they end up being a friend or a foe. Aeduan is the main bad guy we get to see. As a Bloodwitch he is very dangerous as he can control the blood in others bodies and his own. That makes him incredibly hard to kill and extremely powerful. But I can’t help but hold out a little hope that somewhere along the way in this series he decides to be a protector of Safi and Iseult instead of hunting them.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“My life-debt is paid, Threadwitch. If our paths cross again, make no mistake: I will kill you.” <br />“No, you won’t,” she whispered as the door clicked shut. <br />Aeduan forced himself to stay silent. She deserved no response—it would be her mistake if she thought he would spare her.</i>
</blockquote><br />And now I can’t wait for them to meet again and test who will be right.<br /><br />✧ Intense Ending ✧<br /><br />Things were just starting to pick up for me and get really good and then the story was over. This is the bad part about finding a series right when it is starting out. You have to wait for all then next books. But I was ready to jump into the next one right after this finished had it been available.<br /><blockquote>
  <i> All that physical training, Merik had said, plus a witchery men would kill for. Think of all you could do. Think of all you could be.</i>
</blockquote><br />Well I can’t wait to find that out.<br /><br /><b>What might not work for you.</b><br /><br />It took quite a while for this to get really rolling for me and since there isn’t any info dumping I initially kept getting the girls and their powers mixed up until about 30% in. I wish there was an index with the different names of the various types of witchcraft and a few of the characters and or places in the book. There is a pretty good map and that was helpful though.<br /><br />The other thing is this seemed to be pretty character driven for the most part. There is a plot but for me this was a set up book. Here are the main characters that we will be following and a little bit of their history. But there isn’t a huge quest the girls are going on. In fact Safi is only trying to escape her responsibilities and fate for the most of the story. Not in a bad I’m a brat kind of way but more in a I’m just trying to live my life and everyone is out to use me kind of way.<br /><br /><b>Overall</b><br /><br />I’ve really shied away from YA lately because so many of the tropes seem to bug me and they are so overused. Susan Dennard did a great job of telling a story through the eyes of multiple characters and taking the reader on a journey with them. She built tension and drama and gave a lot of hints of things to come in the story without ever treating the reader like they are stupid and need to be told everything up front. She had extraordinary friendships that you believed in not because you are told they are best friends but because through every action and deed the reader sees it. <br /><br />This is definitely an introductory book but I for one look forward to seeing where she takes the story from here.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13591547796145331429" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1268960184" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1268960184" />
    <a title="Rachel E. Carter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29482005-rachel-e-carter"><img alt="Rachel E. Carter" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1512593159p2/29482005.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1268960184?book_show_action=true">May 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel E. Carter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel E. Carter" href="/user/show/29482005-rachel-e-carter">Rachel E. Carter</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29482005-rachel-e-carter?shelf=br">br</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1268960184" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer464022886139342836">First of all: A+++ for those heartthreads and the slow-burn-turned-crazy-hot-tension between Merik and Safi. Best way to describe this? Adult fantasy meets YA. For those of you that love super intricate world building and plot lines, this is your book.<br/><br/>...I read someone's review that said this book was a light fantasy read for people who wanted to read about dresses & balls and that picky fantasy readers would want something more complex. I don't agree. I honestly found the world building in this</span>
  <span id="freeText464022886139342836" style="display:none">First of all: A+++ for those heartthreads and the slow-burn-turned-crazy-hot-tension between Merik and Safi. Best way to describe this? Adult fantasy meets YA. For those of you that love super intricate world building and plot lines, this is your book.<br /><br />...I read someone's review that said this book was a light fantasy read for people who wanted to read about dresses &amp; balls and that picky fantasy readers would want something more complex. I don't agree. I honestly found the world building in this book PHENOMENAL &gt;&gt; like crazy-detailed and layers upon layers of meaning &amp; events that are bringing about a game-changing plot. The first 30% I was honestly struggling just to take the whole world in, it was that complex! This felt waaaaay more adult fantasy (in terms of attention to detail and world-building) so I'd actually argue the opposite: if you want heavy fantasy, read this book. There are plenty of light fantasies I love but I've read enough of those to recognize this as <i>more.</i><br /><br />Ohhhh, and the romance is very, VERY slow burn in the beginning which means you actually learn who the characters are as people and fall for them as who they could be together instead of just giving us one simple glance and poof they have attraction. There was a review that said instalove at the ball. Ummm, I read that same section. The whole awesome dance sequence between Merik and Safi &gt;&gt; never once did I get the feeling of intense attraction, it was more mutual fascination (that was the best dance scene I've ever read, it was like watching a choreographed ballroom dance meets tango lol) and respect (that both could dance so well) and never once did Safi or Merik obsess about the other's eyes/looks/etc during the dance. So, no. No instalove in this book.<br /><br />Let's talk about the friendship: Iseult and Safi. Be real. Name the number of YA fantasy books you've read that spend most of their time focusing on the friendship instead of the romance -even 1% more? I honestly can't. I love a good romance, but I also can seriously appreciate a good friendship -and this book gives readers the friendship that they have been missing. These two were the most important aspect of the series -and they literally balanced each other out (you will understand exactly what this means if you read through to the end). Not only that, but both were flawed and used the other to make each one a better person.</span>
  <a data-text-id="464022886139342836" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1273610198" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1273610198" />
    <a title="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin"><img alt="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603831478p2/17438949.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1273610198?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" href="/user/show/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin">Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/25187640-truthwitch">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin?shelf=fantasy-all">fantasy-all</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1273610198" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13828730557193837660">MY BLOG: <a href='http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2016/01/truthwitch-by-susan-dennard.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Melissa Martin's Reading List</a><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452359551i/17684516._SY540_.jpg' alt=' : ' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>SO HERE WE GO</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448912596i/17205490._SX540_.jpg' alt=' : ' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I was confused at a lot in the book, I'm still confused at some things, but it's all good because what things I did understand were awesome! The two main characters, Safiya and Iseult are Threadsisters. Certain peeps, well witches can bond and become sisters or brothers. Safiya is a Truthwitch and Iseult is a Threadwitch, I don't need to tell you all of this because you can read it in the description of the book. <br/><br/>Anyway, so these two bad-@ssed g</span>
  <span id="freeText13828730557193837660" style="display:none">MY BLOG: <a href="http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2016/01/truthwitch-by-susan-dennard.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Melissa Martin's Reading List</a><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452359551i/17684516._SY540_.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>SO HERE WE GO</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448912596i/17205490._SX540_.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I was confused at a lot in the book, I'm still confused at some things, but it's all good because what things I did understand were awesome! The two main characters, Safiya and Iseult are Threadsisters. Certain peeps, well witches can bond and become sisters or brothers. Safiya is a Truthwitch and Iseult is a Threadwitch, I don't need to tell you all of this because you can read it in the description of the book. <br><br>Anyway, so these two bad-@ssed girls are starting trouble right out of the gate, unfortunately, this put them in the sights of a bloodwitch and he wants them dead. He can track you if he gets a scent of your blood, ewww. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452361282i/17684786._SY540_.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Then a bunch of stuff goes down, political and otherwise and the next thing you know the girls are running for their lives trying to get to a safe haven. Then someone hires Aeduan (the bloodwitch) to get one of the girls back and he owes a debt to the other girl. Yeah, I know, it's all crazeee when I try to explain it, but you will catch on when you read the book :-)<br><br>Back to the girls running for their lives... the girls are running for their lives and end up at their lighthouse (read book) at a standoff with some evil peeps and what not.... then they meet this guy they met awhile back. His name is Merik and he's a Windwitch &lt;---- I hope I got that right because there are so many freaking witches with different names in the book I can't keep them straight. Anyhoo, he gets them onto his boat and off they go. He seems to have a contract for one of the girls as well. I mean geez, every one has contracts out on them! So Merik has a threadbrother named Kullen and they can make crazy wind, hurricanes. etc. They seem all mean and what-not, but they turn out to be good guys. <br><br>Soooo, the majority of the book takes place with all of them traveling on the boat to this other place. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452361282i/17684787._SX540_.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1452361282ra/17684788.gif" alt=" " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>One of the girls is hurt and they need a firewitch to heal her so they are trying to get away from people chasing them, other people chasing them, some sea monsters and trying to figure out how to make a stop for a firewitch. <br><br>Here's a little excerpt about Merik and Kullen <br><br><b>---&gt;EXCERPT&lt;---</b><br><br><b>
  <i>Unlike Merik, Kullen's elemental magic wasn't exclusive to air currents-- he was a full Airwitch, able to control a man's lungs, able to dominate the heat and the storms, and once, he'd even stopped a full-blown hurricane. Witches like Merik were common enough and with varying degrees of mastery over the wind, but as far as Merik knew, Kullen was the only living person with complete control over all aspects of the air.</i>
</b><br><br><u>How cool is that?</u><br><br>There are some other characters in the book that I really like too, but I'm not going into all of that. <br><br>As always in a lot of books I read, people are not always what they seem. There is a lot going on in this book that you will just have to read about yourself. Some really evil person is out there and needs to be stopped, they have a really bad magic that just about destroyed a lot of them. <br><br>Someone did die in the book and it really made me sad :-( <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1446412745ra/16803114.gif" alt=" " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>In the end people are separated and I don't know what is going to happen to everyone. I can't wait to see where the author is taking this story next! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1452361282ra/17684789.gif" alt=" " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>---&gt;EXCERPT&lt;---<br><br><b><i>I guard the light-bringer, <br>And protect the dark-giver. <br>I live for the world-starte, <br>And die for the shadow-ender. <br>My blood, I offer freely. <br>My Threads, I offer wholly. <br>My eternal soul belongs to no one else. <br>Claim my Aether. <br>Guide my blade. <br>From now until the end.</i></b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452361282i/17684790.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="13828730557193837660" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1422179200" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1422179200" />
    <a title="Kiki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4074594-kiki"><img alt="Kiki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545082712p2/4074594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1422179200?book_show_action=true">Oct 21, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kiki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kiki" href="/user/show/4074594-kiki">Kiki</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781447282044" href="/book/show/26802894-truthwitch">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1422179200" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5290527042424309238">Ah, <i>Truthwitch.</i> The truth is, you let me down.<br/><br/>Did you see that? 'The truth is'. Because she's a Truthwitch! So it's like a pun! <br/><br/>You know when you can just feel yourself being really annoying, and you can tell the people around you are getting sick of you, but you just cannot stop? I usually get like that when I'm extremely bored, and so I caught myself doing it a lot as I was reading <i>Truthwitch</i>: knowing that I need to finish this, but being bored out of my mind, and so compelled to scratch away </span>
  <span id="freeText5290527042424309238" style="display:none">Ah, <i>Truthwitch.</i> The truth is, you let me down.<br /><br />Did you see that? 'The truth is'. Because she's a Truthwitch! So it's like a pun! <br /><br />You know when you can just feel yourself being really annoying, and you can tell the people around you are getting sick of you, but you just cannot stop? I usually get like that when I'm extremely bored, and so I caught myself doing it a lot as I was reading <i>Truthwitch</i>: knowing that I need to finish this, but being bored out of my mind, and so compelled to scratch away at the patience of anyone near me until I'm very firmly told to shut up.<br /><br /><i>Truthwitch</i>, for me, absolutely bombed; it was boring, the characters were flat, the prose was weak, and above all, it may as well have been written in Amharic for how well I understood it. <b>This is my absolute number one complaint about this book</b>. I can cope with weird, dull, angry Merik, and Safi who shares my trait of being unable to stop annoying people. I can deal with flat, dreary Iseult and all of the hundreds of thousands of politicians whose names I can't remember. I can cope with the numerous typos, the cliched elemental magic system, and the generic romance. But what I am not willing to overlook is the absolute shambles that is the world-building in this <i>high fantasy</i> novel. <br /><br />Cahr Awen? Origin Wells? Cleaving? The Void? All of these things are very important parts of <i>Truthwitch</i>'s world-building as a whole, but they remain a total mystery at the end of the book. I mean, cleaving is a little clearer, but the rules of it are all over the place, and we never get an explanation of what it actually is and what causes it. Origin Wells? No idea whatsoever. Cahr Awen? What is the Cahr Awen? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I have a feeling that this might be Safi and Iseult's "destiny" but there's never ever any hint as to what that is. Aren't we supposed to know what the fuck the destiny is when the heroes go after it? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Threadfamilies, Threadstones, Threads in general? The Puppeteer? The evil dude in the village with the people and stuff? It's all just walloped at you at warped speed within the first three or so chapters, and honestly, I'm surprised I didn't give up. I was <i>this close</i> to throwing in the towel at around the 200 page mark but I made a commitment to finish every book I start during this reading challenge. No skipping, no switching, and no two books at once. Start one, you finish it.<br /><br />Oh, but there's a catch with that, my friends. After being ahead of the game from the start, I nearly fell behind because this book took me a <i>week</i> to read. Almost all of the books I've started since the beginning of this challenge have taken me two to three days, but this book took me <i>a whole week</i>. I was just to tired of it, so tired that I feel asleep about four times while I was reading it. But here's the thing, and I stand by this: Susan Dennard is a really decent writer. She can construct a scene, write compelling dialogue, and her actions scenes are fun and thrilling. But the plot of this book suffers, because the world-building is so bananas. There's some chasing, and a thing about a wedding and that bloody trade agreement but it all just sort of peters out, and then at the last minute a totally unrelated conflict headed by a totally unrelated villain comes in to play and it was so incredibly random. I felt like I was supposed to be...shocked? I think I was supposed to feel something at the turn of the last page, but it was really just a case of "oh, okay." <br /><br />You could say that about everything in this book. "Oh. Okay." It was just so lacklustre, so repetitive and stuffed with unnecessary charging around. Safi and Iseult and Merik just blast from place to place, and every now and again they'll be like "We're almost there! It's imperative that we reach [location that has never been mentioned before]!" And there's no way to react to that, other than, "Oh. Okay."<br /><br />Amid all of the shouting and the racing around and the relentlessly hurling unexplained fantasy concepts at the reader, this book just falls right on its ass. It wanted to be epic and amazing, and it probably makes sense to some people, but I'm not prepared to make excuses for it. I paid £15 for this, and all I got was a headache and a nap I never asked for. How is that fair?</span>
  <a data-text-id="5290527042424309238" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1174373288" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1174373288" />
    <a title="Lucia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8837962-lucia"><img alt="Lucia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1484242793p2/8837962.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1174373288?book_show_action=true">Jan 20, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lucia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lucia" href="/user/show/8837962-lucia">Lucia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8837962-lucia?shelf=5-stars-read">5-stars-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8837962-lucia?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8837962-lucia?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1174373288" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17307820940733887733">If you are looking for new captivating YA fantasy series, look no further. Here are five reasons that will make Truthwitch your next book-hungover-worthy read.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452842088i/17749871.jpg' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452842088i/17749872.jpg' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452842088i/17749873.jpg' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452842088i/17749874.jpg' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>1. CHARACTERS<br/><br/>Truthwitch has very interesting set of main characters (four different POVs) and every single one of them provided something unique and memorable to make me fall in love with them. Safi, a Truthwitch, is funny and sarcastic, impulsive and unrestrained, fierce and passionate. She has all characteristics that I like to have in e</span>
  <span id="freeText17307820940733887733" style="display:none">If you are looking for new captivating YA fantasy series, look no further. Here are five reasons that will make Truthwitch your next book-hungover-worthy read.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452842088i/17749871.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452842088i/17749872.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452842088i/17749873.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452842088i/17749874.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>1. CHARACTERS<br><br>Truthwitch has very interesting set of main characters (four different POVs) and every single one of them provided something unique and memorable to make me fall in love with them. Safi, a Truthwitch, is funny and sarcastic, impulsive and unrestrained, fierce and passionate. She has all characteristics that I like to have in enjoyable female heroine. Iseult, a Threadwitch, is calm and smart, perceptive and logical, always thinking things through. And she is the best and the most loyal friend you could ask for. Merik, a Windwitch, is fierce and temperamental, but capable admiral/dancer and loyal friend/prince trying to save his country. He captured my heart early in the story and his impression on me never faltered. Aeduan, a Bloodwitch, is cold and dark, mysterious and deadly. He has this strong villain-y vibe going on and I’m incredibly curious to see where author will take his character in next instalments.<br><br>2. WORLD-BUILDING<br><br>This novel shows why I love fantasies. There is no better to spend my free time than losing myself in new world and its specific politics, history, legends, religions and culture. It brings my imagination alive. And Truthwitch hit all the right marks for me because its world-building was fascinating, flawless and detailed (fortunately there was no info-dump, it was all revealed gradually when it was needed). Simply said, my inner fantasy nerd was in heaven.<br><br>3. FRIENDSHIP<br><br>Truthwitch is without a doubt the best YA fantasy novel with strong focus on female friendship. Safi &amp; Iseult are from different parts of society and have completely different background. However, they complement each other perfectly and together create lovable team of adventurous witches whose escapades were such a thrilling experience to read about.<br><br>4. CHEMISTRY<br><br>Truthwitch is book with scorching chemistry. Nothing graphics needs to happen, yet the couple (and I am not going to tell you what couple to keep it spoiler-free) could ignite the pages just with simple looks, banters or touch here and there. It shows author’s mastery of writing when she can make me all hot and bothered with butterflies in my stomach *cough* dance scene *cough* while keeping it PG-13.<br><br>5. ACTION<br><br>In Truthwitch, you won’t find love triangle, insta-love or annoying tropes. But you will get perfectly paced storyline with something exciting happening all the time. I was unable to tear my eyes from this novel. Truthwitch is what I call a real page-turner and since I haven’t read one in months, I’m very grateful for this book. Thank you Susan Dennard!<br><br>Truthwitch is a very promising start to new YA fantasy series. It has all three aspects that I require in good fantasy novel (world-building, storytelling, characters) mastered perfectly and I can’t wait to get my hands on sequel!<br><br>MORE REVIEWS ON MY BLOG <a href="http://readingismybreathing.blogspot.cz/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>Reading Is My Breathing</b>
</a></span>

<div id="review_2100632860" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2100632860" />
    <a title="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68538597-booksofradiance"><img alt="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513125058p2/68538597.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2100632860?book_show_action=true">Feb 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" class="user" itemprop="url" name="❄️BooksofRadiance❄️" href="/user/show/68538597-booksofradiance">❄️BooksofRadiance❄️</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/25187640-truthwitch">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68538597-booksofradiance?shelf=ya-fantasy-sci-fi">ya-fantasy-sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2100632860" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16530892587694236015">3.75⭐️<br/><br/>Now that’s what I call a pleasant little surprise. <br/><br/>I loved this book. The reason why it’d taken me an entire year to finally decide to read it was because I’d already banked on it disappointing me. What a mistake that was. <br/><br/>I loved the overall plot and were it not for the gross lack of world building, it would’ve been a solid 4.5⭐️ read.<br/>But what it lacked in the WB, it more than made up for it with its characters. <br/>AMZING CHARACTERS! Each one more intriguing than the previous, particularly t</span>
  <span id="freeText16530892587694236015" style="display:none">3.75⭐️<br /><br />Now that’s what I call a pleasant little surprise. <br /><br />I loved this book. The reason why it’d taken me an entire year to finally decide to read it was because I’d already banked on it disappointing me. What a mistake that was. <br /><br />I loved the overall plot and were it not for the gross lack of world building, it would’ve been a solid 4.5⭐️ read.<br />But what it lacked in the WB, it more than made up for it with its characters. <br />AMZING CHARACTERS! Each one more intriguing than the previous, particularly the four main characters (obviously). <br /><br />And of course, I can’t wrap this up without mentioning one of the great highlights of this novel - the great and empowering friendships, not only between the two female leads but also between two other male characters. <br />For once there was no girl-on-girl hate, no petty jealous rivalry or unfounded bitchyness, just an incredibly powerful, lean-on-me-I’ll-lean-on-you kind of friendships that we unfortunately very seldom see, particularly in YA. Both in fantasy and contemporary. <br /><br /><b>My biggest drawback: The lack of world building.</b><br /><br />The book is written in a way that implies that the reader already has a vast knowledge of the world that’s introduced. <br />We’re constantly reminded of all sorts of conflicts between the different kingdoms (three of four) and strong prejudices against some tribal nations yet there’s little context behind these conflicts and no origin story whatsoever. NOTHING IS EXPLAINED. <br /><br />It was as if SD expected us to have already known everything - the world, the inner machinations and politics of all the kingdoms, the hows and whys of the magic system, why there’re many prejudices against some of the weaker nations and tribal factions, and more importantly, the details behind the 20-year (or was it 10? I don’t remember) truce that is about to come to an end. <br /><br />I’m hoping book two will shed some light into some of these questions, at the very least, because I’d hate for my love for this (promising) series to be tainted simply by a lack of explanation. <br /><br />All in all, a surprisingly refreshing read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16530892587694236015" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1440855789" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1440855789" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577914102p2/3030788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1440855789?book_show_action=true">Nov 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=witches">witches</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=signed">signed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1440855789" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer149368976591986094"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380412808ra/811980.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1453332747i/17813573._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>ARC provided by the publisher via Netgalley in exchange for an honest review.</i><br/><br/>I actually received an "Extended Extract ARC" for this book. So basically, the first half of this review is going to be my opinions on chapters one through fifteen that were given to me for review. Then, I will tell you the rest of my thoughts on the book, now that it is officially released and I have bought it for chapters sixteen through forty. The fifteen chapters I did review, for Netgalley, were amazing. Easily one</span>
  <span id="freeText149368976591986094" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380412808ra/811980.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1453332747i/17813573._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>ARC provided by the publisher via Netgalley in exchange for an honest review.</i><br><br>I actually received an "Extended Extract ARC" for this book. So basically, the first half of this review is going to be my opinions on chapters one through fifteen that were given to me for review. Then, I will tell you the rest of my thoughts on the book, now that it is officially released and I have bought it for chapters sixteen through forty. The fifteen chapters I did review, for Netgalley, were amazing. Easily one of my favorite reads for 2015. So I was very excited for my signed copy to get here from <a href="http://www.booksofwonder.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Books of Wonder</a>, because I was really confident that I would love it based on the fifteen chapter ARC I received.<br><br><b>
  <u>Review for Chapters 1-15:</u>
</b><br>The main theme of this book is friendship and what two young women can accomplish with it. It's always so refreshing for me to read about a strong woman, but <b>two</b> is such a rarity. And they are actually best friends, and not catty and competitive with one another. This is so rare in YA, and I hope this starts a movement with more authors writing about how wonderful girl friendships can be. The only other series I can think of that also has an amazing girl/girl friendship is <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1250009402" rel="nofollow noopener">Cracked</a>, and I absolutely adored that book as well. <br><br>In this world there are five Origin Wells that are spread across the Witchlands. Each Well is based off a major element --Aether, Earth, Water, Wind, or Fire. There is also a Void element that most people think is a myth, because they have no records of a Void Well. Every person in this world is a type of witch that derives from one of these elements. Like, there are so many different kinds of witches, it was insane. You have the basic Earthwitches and Firewitches, but you also have Voicewitches and Tidewitches. So basically your powers can be very broad or very focused. <br><br>The two best friends in this book have very different powers, but both of their powers are very unique. Iseult (my favorite of the two) is a Threadwitch, which means she can see other's threads/outcomes. She cannot see her own or other Threadwitches, but she can see their intentions from different colors that appear. Safi is a Truthwitch that can obviously tell the truth from a lie (unless someone has a crazy amount of power to mask it). The special thing about her being a Truthwitch is that the last recorded one died a century ago. This makes Safi very valuable, especially with an upcoming Truth Summit.<br><br>The world building for this blew me away. There are three empires in this book that have a treaty for twenty years of peace. Well, that is about to end and a big Truth Summit is about to take place that will probably not end with much peace. This is why it's so important for Safi to keep her magic hidden, because she could easily become a captive pawn in this game when so much will be at stake. <br><br>Both Safi and Iseult are good-hearted little trouble makers. After a run-in where they lose their money, they try to get a little revenge. Unfortunately for them, a Bloodwitch named Aeduan ends up putting them on his radar. Bloodwitches are another type of witch that is very rare and mostly unheard of anymore. Bloodwitches can smell a person's blood and track them forever, so there is not much question on why they are so valuable, and now he's on a mission to find these two troublemakers. They are also almost impossible to kill, because the only way is to completely sever the head from the body. Aeduan being able to track Safi is a huge problem the two girls are trying to overcome. Aeduan also has smelled Iseult 's blood <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[and it's the only blood he's ever smelled that did not have a scent <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Both girls soon realize that Bloodwitches can also manipulate blood, which is probably the most powerful magic I had read about yet. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[It was also very apparent to me (especially with the ending of Chapter Fifteen), that Aeduan will be Iseult's love interest, and ohhhhmyyygawwwd do I ship that. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>The girls split up and you get to see how different their lives are separated from one another. Safi lives a much wealthier life, with a very powerful Uncle. You also see hints and glimpses that the rest of Safi's family is not around, but you never find out why <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[but you do know that they were killed and her Uncle was not <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. She attends a ball and realizes more people are aware of her unusual power than what she originally thought. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[She also totally meets her love interest, Prince Merik. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Iseult comes from a witch tribe of Threadwitches that are lead by a man named Corlant, who is pretending to be one <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[even though he is truly a Cursewitch. Cursewitches are also a witchcraft linked to the Void that seems very, very powerful  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Iseult makes her way home once she is separated from Safi. Iseult reunites with her mother, another friend of hers, and her dog. Sadly the homecoming is short lived, because Corlant convinces the witch tribe that Iseult is the Puppeteer, which is something unknown and they all fear, and wants them to kill her because of it. <i>Man, maybe Donald Trump, or the people who plan on voting for him, should read this book.</i> <br><br>The half of this book that I was able to read was a breath of fresh air. I think it will speak to many readers on many ends of many spectrums. I think there is something likeable for everyone, and it will be very easy for readers to connect with. I don't want to sound like a broken record, but the female friendship was beyond refreshing, and an absolute joy to read about. I want much more of this story. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[And much more Iseult and Aeduan, because <i>holy shit</i> that Chapter Fifteen cliffhanger! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>
  <u>Review for Chapters 16-40:</u>
</b><br>I went into this thinking I would lower my originally five star rating, because I thought something would happen to upset me, irritate me, or cast away the spell this book has put my heart under. That never happened, if anything, these following chapters helped me love this world more. The characters are fantastic, the world building blew me away (especially for a first book in a series), and the plot is original and mesmerizing. That last chapter even tied in with the first chapter, involving the Chiseled Cheater, and that is another surefire way to make sure your book makes it into my heart.<br><br>This book also introduces "sex foxes" with are totally glorified sirens; which is a huge guilty pleasure/weakness for me. It was a wonderful take on them, and like I said, I'm just smitten for mythical creatures that lure men to their deaths. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1452140560ra/17651499.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I thought I was so in love with Iseult and Aeduan's story line, until I read the rest of this book and realized how freakin' in love I am with Safi and Merik. They are totally reminding me of Cleo and Magnus in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1455382903" rel="nofollow noopener">Falling Kingdoms</a>, with the "I love to hate you" romances, that somehow just work for me. I couldn't get enough of them in the last half of this book. Then, Safi's "deal" with Vaness and the surprise in Merik's jacket.... be still, my heart. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/511183.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Aeduan is even more complex that I imagined in the first fifteen chapters. He surprises me left and right with his <s>thoughtfulness</s> life-debts <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[and his past with Evrane blew me away! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I'm nervous and excited to learn about his father in the next book.<br><br>Evrane was an amazing new character, and her shedding light on the truth about the Cahr Awen definitely opens up the story a little more. Or, it like, breaks down the wall for a million story arcs now.<br><br>Iseult's role was smaller in the last half of this book, just because she was sick <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[thanks to the cursed arrow from Corlant <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> a lot, and mostly just healing. I still enjoyed her character and her devotion to her friendship with her Threadsister. <br><br>It's only January 6th and, without a doubt, this book is going to make it on my "Best of 2016" list come December. This book truly proves that <i>"friendships can be just as epic as romances"</i> and we need a whole lot of that in this world. I would recommend this to everyone. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380412156ra/810425.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://meltotheany.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany/profile" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1507893285" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2359047299281252683"><u>FULL REVIEW POSTED</u><br/><br/>Can I just get a big HELL YES because this has been one of the only books I have genuinely enjoyed in a while and im v impressed by susan Dennard, you got me interested, lady, im coming back for more<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1508204970i/24190423._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><a href='https://freiheit.deviantart.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>(s)</a> <br/><br/>-	The world, while confusing initially, is really thought out and developed <br/>-	Culture, history, politics, magic, all really well done<br/>-	I really enjoyed how the plot was intricate and the story revolved around that<br/>-	There were multiple POVS (yes!!!) and they all became connected </span>
  <span id="freeText2359047299281252683" style="display:none"><u>FULL REVIEW POSTED</u><br><br>Can I just get a big HELL YES because this has been one of the only books I have genuinely enjoyed in a <div id="review_1267621355" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1267621355" />
    <a title="Maria V. Snyder" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1629797-maria-v-snyder"><img alt="Maria V. Snyder" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530814046p2/1629797.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1267621355?book_show_action=true">Apr 29, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria V. Snyder" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria V. Snyder" href="/user/show/1629797-maria-v-snyder">Maria V. Snyder</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1267621355" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14359276365712174507">I received the manuscript for this book from the editor - she was hoping I'd enjoy it enough to give it a blurb. I really liked the book - the beginning was a little hard for me to get into, mainly because the two protagonists do something I thought was foolish. However it was important to show how the two characters grow and change during the course of the story so it didn't prevent me from reading the rest of the book. And once past that, I was sucked into the story.<br/><br/>The plot is hard to describ</span>
  <span id="freeText14359276365712174507" style="display:none">I received the manuscript for this book from the editor - she was hoping I'd enjoy it enough to give it a blurb. I really liked the book - the beginning was a little hard for me to get into, mainly because the two protagonists do something I thought was foolish. However it was important to show how the two characters grow and change during the course of the story so it didn't prevent me from reading the rest of the book. And once past that, I was sucked into the story.<br /><br />The plot is hard to describe - it's the first book of a fantasy series. In the world, there are various types of witches and the two main protagonists are both witches - Safiya is a Truthwitch, she can tell when someone isn't being truthful and Iseult is a Threadwitch, she can see a person's threads which relate to their moods. Although the young women aren't related, they are thread sisters, which means they have a strong bond that goes beyond friendship. In the beginning of the story, they encounter a Bloodwitch, who can smell a person's blood and then track that person and he can also heal and is almost impossible to kill. Well the Bloodwitch is after Safiya and Iseult and they go on the run. There's a political element - the countries have all signed a treaty not to wage war for 20 years and that time is almost up.<br /><br />As I said I enjoyed it and gave this blurb: "Truthwitch has it all, strong female characters, adventure, magic, romance, and non-stop action that will leave you breathless!"</span>
  <a data-text-id="14359276365712174507" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
